පාර්ලිෙම්න්තුව 3403 3404

Mr. Deputy Chairman, the internationally acclaimed American Writer Mark Twain once said, I quote: “When in doubt, tell the truth”. Today, I am before you to tell the truth about the doubts that I, and Members of the Sri Lanka Muslim Congress had been entertaining during the past several months, as Ministers and Members of the ruling coalition. However, I should emphasize the fact that it is with no malice or acrimony that I present my case and that of my Party and we will continue to maintain very healthy ties with President Mahinda Rajapaksa and his Ministers and Members of the Government even in the future despite our decision to leave the Government. There are no hostilities between us. We have only parted ways on principles. We behaved in the most diplomatic manner possible in the process of leaving the Government. As we promised, we have given adequate advance notice on our decision to quit the Government and we expect the Government too to respond to our departure in a similar mature manner and take it in the spirit that we have made this move. All of you are aware the circumstances under which we became part of the Government. The decision was more to do with keeping the unity of the party, than out of conviction that there would be room within this Government, with its assortment of parties, for us to get at least some leg space to get the basic demands of the Muslim community, met. As the leader of the Party, I had serious misgivings about the capability of this Government, with its far right wing slant, to address the grievances of minorities - both Muslims and Tamils - from the very outset. My Friends in Parliament and outside are witnesses to the fact that even on the day I joined the Government - 28th January, 2007 to be precise - I shared my doubts and dilemmas with them. I told them that my stint in this Government is not going to last long and it is to prevent a split in the party that I was joining the Government. If one peruses through the media interviews given by me during several months it will become clear that I have been maintaining this stance in almost all my media comments. Despite all these uncertainties about the manner the Government would approach the Muslim grievances, we were dignified enough to abide by the collective responsibility. We defended the Government in the House and outside throughout our stint, even putting the party’s credibility at stake on many occasions. It is true there were times that I had exercised my right to dissent on many occasions as well but, however we exercised the right to dissent with dignity and decorum. Finally at the

Second Reading of the Budget we kept our word and voted for the Budget. While we were dutifully playing our part as an ally of the Government, we were very much conscious of the growing restlessness among our own constituents. The delicate politics in the East, and as a matter of fact also among Muslims outside the North and the East, is in such a situation that everyday new issues keep on cropping up. There is slew of issues pertaining to land, security, economic interest and our right to exercise our religious freedom. In the case of land issues, our people are facing a type of problems that they have never faced before making them feel that they are outcasts in their own lands. On the other hand, the Northern Muslims who have been languishing in Puttalam and in several other neighbouring areas for seventeen long years are now expected to return to their places of origin without any security guarantees, due to fear psychosis among some Members of the Government that a long-term presence of my people in Puttalam would disturb the traditional demographic pattern of the area. ெகளரவ பிரதித் தவிசாளர் அவர்கேள, இடம்ெபயர்ந்த வடᾗல ᾙஸ்ᾢம்கள் இன்ᾠ மிகᾫம் பாிதாபகரமான சூழ்நிைலயில் இᾞக்கின்றார்கள் என்பᾐ தங்கᾦக்குத் ெதாிᾜம். அந்த வடᾗல மக்கள் அங்கு மீளக் குᾊயமர்வதற்கான ஒᾞ சுᾙகமான சூழ்நிைல அைமகின்ற வைர மீள்குᾊேயற்ற விஷயத்திேல அரசாங்கம் அந்த மக்கைள எந்த விதத்திᾤம் வற்ᾗᾠத்தாமல் நடந்ᾐெகாள்ளேவண்ᾌம் என்ᾠ பல தடைவ ᾯ லங்கா ᾙஸ்ᾢம் காங்கிரஸ் மிகᾫம் பணிவாகᾫம் விநயமாகᾫம் ேவண்ᾊ வந்திᾞக்கின்றᾐ. அந்த மக்களின் நலᾔக்காகᾫம் ேமம்பாட்ᾊற்காகᾫம் அைமக்கப்பட்ட இவ்வைமச்சின் வரᾫ-ெசலᾫத் திட்டக் குᾨநிைல விவாதத்திேல இந்தக் கᾞத்ᾐக்கைள மீண்ᾌெமாᾞதடைவ நான் இங்கு ெசால்ᾢக் ெகாள்ள விᾞம்ᾗகின்ேறன். அவர்கᾦக்கு எந்தவிதப் பாᾐகாப்ᾗம் இல்லாத சூழᾢல், அவர்கᾦைடய ஜீவாதாரத்திற்கு, இயல்ᾗ வாழ்க்ைகக்குச் சாியான உத்தரவாதங்கள் இல்லாத நிைலயில் அவசரப்பᾌத்தி அவர்கைள மீள்குᾊேயற்றம் ெசய்வைதவிᾌத்ᾐ, எல்லா அரசியல் தரப்ᾗக்கேளாᾌம், அதாவᾐ நியாயᾘர்வமாக நடந்ᾐெகாள்கின்ற எல்லா இன ஜனநாயக அரசியல் தைலைமகேளாᾌம் ேபசி, ஒᾞ சாியான அரசியல் பின்ᾗலத்திேல அவர்கைள மீள்குᾊேயற்ᾠவᾐதான் சாத்தியமானᾐ என்ᾠம் நாங்கள் பல தடைவகள் இந்த அரசிடம் பணிவாகᾫம் விநயமாகᾫம் ேகாாி வந்திᾞக்கின்ேறாம். அப்பᾊயிᾞந்தேபாதிᾤம் பல சமயங்களிேல எங்கᾦைடய நியாயᾘர்வமான ேகாாிக்ைககள் நியாயத் தன்ைமேயாᾌ பார்க்கப்படவில்ைல என்பᾐகுறித்ᾐ நான் மிகᾫம் மனம் ெநாந்திᾞக்கின்ேறன். இதனால்தான் ᾯ லங்கா ᾙஸ்ᾢம் காங்கிரஸ் பாராᾦமன்ற உᾠப்பினர்கள் இவ்வாறான ஒᾞ ᾙᾊைவ எᾌப்பதற்கு எங்கᾦைடய அரசியல் உச்ச பீடம் அதிகாரம் அளித்திᾞக்கின்றᾐ. அந்த அᾊப்பைடயிேலதான் நாங்கள் இந்த ᾙᾊᾫக்கு வந்திᾞக்கின்ேறாம். இந்த ᾙᾊᾫ ஏன் எᾌக்கப்பட்டᾐ? Mr. Deputy Chairman, as a result of all these things, during the last few months my Party came under tremendous pressure from the Muslim community to withdraw our support to the Government as there was absolutely no hope for the community in the horizon under the present regime. The unpalatable reality about the Government is that its composition and power alignment are such that it can make very little progress in addressing the grievances of the minorities, not only Muslims equally those of Tamils. Even though a few may make some genuine efforts to resolve some of the issues, those moves too are doomed to fall apart due to the imbalanced power configuration. Here, I must very emphatically say, that we have no differences with the Sri Lanka Freedom Party and its policies. It is my duty, Mr. Deputy Chairman, with the same dignity and decorum to thank the Hon. Members of this Government, His Excellency the President, the Hon. Prime Minister, the Hon. It is not that he did not try to keep us within this fold but I know, he utterly failed. With those words, I thank once again all my Colleagues in this Government and wish them all the very best. We are discussing, Sir, the Votes of the Ministry of Disaster Management and Human Rights. I would respectfully state that I think the biggest disaster that the Hon. Minister has to manage today is the human rights situation in this country. That, I think is the biggest disaster he is confronted with and which he has to manage. Before I proceed further, Sir, to deal with the question of human rights in this country, I would like to read from a publication of the UN, in regard to the struggle for human rights. That publication states" “Each violation of human rights, wherever it occurs is a threat to the welfare and dignity of the entire human family. The protection of human rights therefore is a worldwide responsibility which transcends all racial, ideological and geographical boundaries. This is the fundamental belief which has given birth to the international struggle for human rights”. Therefore, Sir, might I state that the human rights situation in this country is not merely a concern for this country but a concern for the whole world. Today, we have begun to see that the world, the international community in particular, is beginning to show their concern in a very grave and serious way in regard to the human rights situation that prevails in this country. නිෙයෝජɕ සභාපතිතුමා (பிரதித் தவிசாளர் அவர்கள்) (The Deputy Chairman) කරුණාකර ගරු මන්තීතුමන්ලා තමන්ෙග් ආසනවලට යන්න. ගරු ආර්. සම්පන්දන් මහතා (மாண்ᾗமிகு ஆர். சம்பந்தன்) (The Hon. “Whereas it is essential, if man is not to be compelled to have recourse, as a last resort, to rebellion against tyranny and oppression, that human rights should be protected by the rule of law” In this country, Sir, we are in a situation where certainly human rights are not being protected by the rule of law. Members, Sir, to keep quiet ? - [Interruption.] Please! - [Interruption.] Might I appeal to the Chair to ask the Hon. Members to let me speak ? නිෙයෝජɕ සභාපතිතුමා (பிரதித் தவிசாளர் அவர்கள்) (The Deputy Chairman) ගරු මහින්දානන්ද අලුත්ගමෙග් ඇමතිතුමා, කරුණාකර නිශ්ශබ්ද ෙවන්න. ගරු ආර්. සම්පන්දන් මහතා (மாண்ᾗமிகு ஆர். சம்பந்தன்) (The Hon. R. Sampanthan) Sir, if they take my time - [Interruption.] They must give me time. Please, do not disturb me. - [Interruption.] I want to say, Sir, that the main reason for the human rights situation in this country being so bad is that the most fundamental human right of the Tamil-speaking people, the Tamil people in particular has not been recognized in this country in the past 50 years. That is, the right to internal self-determination in their areas of historical habitation, which is their fundamental birth right, an inalienable right inherent to those people who bear a distinct identity and who have occupied a certain part of this country. It is the failure to recognize the right to internal self-determination in their areas of historical habitation, which is recognized by the International Covenant on Civil and Political Rights and by the International Covenant on Economic, Social and Cultural Rights, I emphasize, is the main reason for the situation we face in regard to human rights. Before I proceed further, Sir, I would like to quote from the Constitution of this country. I consider the Constitution of Sri Lanka to be an albatross, something very oppressive and which needs fundamental changes. This Constitution needs to undergo a paradigm shift in regard to its structure of governance, but, nevertheless, what does the Constitution state? It states, Sir, in Article 3, I quote: "In the Republic of Sri Lanka sovereignty is in the people and is inalienable. Sovereignty includes the powers of government,...." That is the Legislative power, the Executive power and the judicial power. ".....fundamental rights and the franchise." So, sovereignty also includes human rights. All governments in all countries have invariably enshrined in

their Constitutions a chapter on fundamental rights very often, frequently, based upon the Universal Declaration of Human Rights accepted by the UN General Assembly. Different countries may differ. Therefore, the point I want to make is that in terms of your Constitution the expression "sovereignty" also incorporates fundamental rights; it also incorporates human rights. When human rights is under attack in any country, it means that sovereignty is under attack in that country, that sovereignty is no longer a robust whole, on the contrary, it is under pressure; it is under attack and if it continues to be under pressure and if it continues to be under attack- නිෙයෝජɕ සභාපතිතුමා (பிரதித் தவிசாளர் அவர்கள்) (The Deputy Chairman)

ெகளரவ உᾠப்பினர் அவர்கேள, ெகாஞ்சம் அைமதியாக

இᾞங்கள்! කරුණාකර, මූලාසනය සඳහා ගරු ෙර්ණුකා ෙහේරත් මන්තීතුමියෙග් නම ෙයෝජනා කරන්න. ගරු ඩලස් අලහප්ෙපරුම මහතා (පවාහන අමාතɕතුමා) (மாண்ᾗமிகு டலஸ் அலஹப்ெபᾞம - ேபாக்குவரத்ᾐ அைமச்சர்) (The Hon. Dullas Alahapperuma- Minister of Transport) "ගරු ෙර්ණුකා ෙහේරත් මන්තීතුමිය මූලාසනය ගත යුතුය"යි මා ෙයෝජනා කරනවා. පශ්නය විමසන ලදින්, සභා සම්මත විය. வினா விᾌக்கப்பட்ᾌ ஏற்ᾠக்ெகாள்ளப்பட்டᾐ. Question put, and agreed to. අනතුරුව නිෙයෝජɕ කාරක සභාපතිතුමා මූලාසනෙයන් ඉවත් වුෙයන්, ගරු ෙර්ණුකා ෙහේරත් මහත්මිය මුලාසනාරූඪ විය.

அதன்பிறகு, குᾨக்களின் பிரதித் தவிசாளர் அவர்கள் அக்கிராசனத்தினின்ᾠ அகலேவ, மாண்ᾗமிகு (திᾞமதி) ேரᾎகா ேஹரத் அவர்கள் தைலைம வகித்தார்கள். Whereupon MR. DEPUTY CHAIRMAN OF COMMITTEES left the Chair, and THE HON. (MRS.) RENUKA HERATH took the Chair. ගරු ආර්. සම්පන්දන් මහතා (மாண்ᾗமிகு ஆர். சம்பந்தன்) (The Hon. R. Sampanthan) Madam Chairperson, if sovereignty continues to be under attack in a country on the ground that human rights is under attack it would mean that that sovereignty cannot continue to be one robust, holistic whole. It must fragment; it will fragment. That will be inevitable and then we will have a situation where the sovereignty has got to be shared. Perhaps, different people will also be entitled to exercise sovereignty. That will be the position. If you continue to deny the right of internal self-determination to a people who have a distinct identity, who have historically inhabited a certain part of this country, it is inevitable that your sovereignty must crumble and when your sovereignty crumbles, it is inevitable that your sovereignty will have to be shared with someone else, with those people who will be entitled to exercise their own sovereignty. Before I proceed any further, Madam, on this very point, I would like to read from a letter that the late Prime Minister of India, Shrimati Indira Gandhi wrote to President Richard Nixon on 15th December, 1971 in regard to the situation that then prevailed in Bangladesh - then, there were the East Pakistan and the West Pakistan - when it was just being created. This is what she said, I quote: “ The fact of the matter is that the rulers of West Pakistan got away with the impression that they could do what they liked, because no one, not even the United States, would choose to take a public position that

[ගරු ආර්. සම්පන්දන් මහතා]

2007 ෙදසැම්බර් 12 3409 3410

while Pakistan’s integrity was certainly sacrosanct human rights, liberty were no less so, and that there was a necessary inter-connection between the inviolability of states and the contentment of their people.” So, if you continue to keep a people continuously in a state of discontentment, denying them of their most fundamental, inalienable human right - the right to internal self-determination - it is inevitable, Madam, that your sovereignty will be under attack. You might well remember what happened in East Pakistan, which was a part of Pakistan, as a result of that and this situation has also happened in other parts of the world. Having said that, Madam, I would like to refer now briefly to the human rights situation that prevails in this country. It is appalling; it is deplorable - there are massive killings and disappearances, persons are being abducted, persons have no freedom, there is large scale aerial bombing, there is large scale artillery fire, multi-barrel rockets are being fired into civilian populated areas, people are being killed in large numbers, civilian property is being destroyed, houses, plantations, crops, livestock, everything is being destroyed and people are being rendered destitute. They are compelled to go into refugee camps in various parts of the Northern and Eastern Provinces and thousands of people have been killed, hundreds of thousands of people have been displaced both in the North and the East. I propose to give you a brief account of that before I proceed further with my speech. Around 3,900 people were killed in the North-East in 2006 and in the first quarter of 2007, over 700 people were killed in the North-East. These were largely Tamils. They were killed by aerial bombardment, multi-barrel rocket fire, extrajudicial killings by the armed forces and paramilitary groups collaborating with the armed forces. In about the past one year, over 1,000 people, mostly Tamil civilians, are believed to have disappeared. Individual Tamils, two Tamil Parliamentarians, two ex-Tamil Parliamentarians, Tamil members of the clergy, Tamil academics, leading Tamil businessmen, Tamil journalists, Tamil civil society activists, Tamil aid workers employed by international and domestic Non-Governmental Organizations, Tamil students, Tamil civilians seeking refuge in places of worship and other Tamil civilians have been targeted and killed by the armed forces and by paramilitary groups collaborating with the armed forces. The objective of attacks on religious leaders, journalists and civil society activists is to silence such persons and thereby, prevent the exposure of serious human rights abuses. The Government, we are sorry to say, has not been able to take any action to curb this situation. Madam, recently there has been a publication put out by the Law and Society Trust which has done some research, a study on this question in collaboration with four local partners including the Civil Monitoring Commission and the Free Media Movement. They have found that 662 persons have been killed and 540 persons have disappeared during the period 1st January to 31st August, 2007, in a matter of eight months, the number totalling to 1,202, roughly five victims per day. Copies of this document together with their details have been sent to the Presidential Commission of Inquiry dealing with the abductions and disappearances, the Hon. Minister of Disaster Management and Human Rights, the Human Rights Commission and the Attorney-General. In particular, we wish to focus on the fact that the adequacy and propriety of the investigations conducted into these incidents need to be looked at very carefully because there has hardly been any proper investigation done in regard to these several incidents.

I also wish to quote, Madam, from yet another document which has been prepared by several NGOs. "Since the signing of the CFA an approximate total killed amounts to 4,186 in the North and East, with approximately 3,685 killed in the Northern and Eastern provinces from October 2005-May 2007. Whilst exact figures are hard to obtain, other reports from 2005 up to date show an estimated 346 killed/ 533 wounded in 2005, 3,900 killed/ 4,000 wounded in 2006 (with 3,500 killed in the second quarter of 2006 alone) and 705 killed/ 721 wounded in the first quarter of 2007." This is the position, Madam, in regard to the killings that have been going on. In regard to Jaffna, I got some figures this morning from my Friends who are Members of Parliament for Jaffna, since April 2006 up to September, 2007, almost daily two, three or four persons have been killed. About 50 civilians have been killed in a month. Particularly, youth have been targeted by the armed forces and by paramilitary groups. One hundred and ninety three civilians fearing death have sought the protection of the Human Rights Commission in Jaffna and they are presently in custody in the jail in Jaffna for their protection. That is the position in regard to Human Rights. In regard to displacement, according to the reports of various human rights organizations, since August, 2006, 315,000 people fled from their homes in the Eastern Province and 100,000 people in March, 2007 alone. These staggering figures are in addition to the 200,000 to 250,000 people displaced by the tsunami in 2004 and not yet resettled and 315,000 people displaced by the conflict prior to 2002, who also have not yet been resettled in the North and the East. That is in regard to the Eastern Province and what is the position in regard to the North? In the Jaffna District the number of families displaced is 37,631 comprising of 130,248 people. In the Mannar District it is 6,328 families comprising of 23,662 people. In the Vavuniya District it is 3,027 families comprising of 10,643 members and in the Mullaitivu and the Kilinochchi Districts the total number of families displaced is a little over 16,000 and the number of members of families displaced is 83,364 totalling to 247,917 people displaced in the Northern Province in recent times. With the 315,000 people who have been displaced in the Eastern Province as a result of the recent actions of the Government since about August last year, apart from the persons displaced in the earlier period of war and the persons displaced as a result of tsunami, around 600,000 Tamil civilians have been displaced and are living in refugee camps, or with their friends and relations in other places, with hardly any facilities - short of food, short of drinking water, no sanitation and suffering immense deprivation. Sometimes they are being compelled by the Government, against their wish, to return to areas where there is no security. It is an inhuman situation, Madam, that prevails in these areas. I must say that a large number of these people have been displaced as a result of aerial bombardment and multi-barrel rocket launcher fire and that the Government is acting with callous disregard for the safety of the Tamil civilian population. They have no occupation; they have no fishing; they have no farming; they do not have their livestock; they are unable to derive an income; they are unable to survive; the children do not go to school, they have no education and these people are undergoing immense human suffering as a result of the actions of the Government. High Security Zones have been declared. In the Mutur area a High Security Zones has been newly created. There is ethnic cleansing. The Government claimed that they were conducting military operations against the LTTE to free the Tamil people from the clutches of the LTTE. What have

පාර්ලිෙම්න්තුව 3411 3412

you done now? You have destroyed their homes, their plantations, their crops, their livestock, their fishing and farming equipment and you say, “You cannot go back to your lands and live” and the people are being prevented from getting back to the properties in which they have lived for generations and centuries and they are living in a state of utter penury and destitution. What else is this but downright ethnic cleansing, displacement of Tamil people in order to make sure that the Tamil people do not return to those areas. The Hon. Rauff Hakeem happened to remark in the course of his speech, I could not agree with him less, that there is no rule of law in this country, that there is a state of lawlessness that prevails in this country. That is the true position Sir, in regard to the current situation of this country. I must also in this context, Sir, refer to a newspaper article under the heading, "LST claims east not liberated but militarized", which quotes the Report of the Law and Society Trust that has been published recently in regard to the position of the Eastern Province. I quote: "Killings, disappearances and abductions of persons persist in the highly militarized environment of Trincomalee and Mutur, while thousands languish in welfare camps seeking adequate food, shelter and protection.” Are you not ashamed of yourselves to allow people to languish in this way seeking adequate food, shelter and protection? I further quote the newspaper article: “Despite claims of liberation and reawakening of the East, civilians in Trincomalee live in a highly militarized environment. Despite the heavy presence of security forces, disappearances and killings continue regularly," the LST said in the report based on a field visit. The Article goes on, I quote: "Citing the Human Rights Commission, (HRC) Trincomalee office, the report noted that abductions and disappearances were reported almost daily with 24 cases in August and 39 in September. "Many incidents go unreported as no formal complaint is made to the HRC or Police due to fear of reprisals.” the report notes while adding that Trincomalee remains heavily militarized and tense with the town deserted after 7 p.m. It said though the HRC intervened on some violations, it failed to make any notable impact, while HRC investigations into the killing of the five students in January 2006, 17 AFC aid workers in August, 2006 and Ven. Nandarathna thera in Trnicomalee had reached a standstill.” Ven. Nandarathna thero, Sir, was one of the Buddhist priests who was very friendly, who got along on very well with the Tamil people and who was shot dead for that reason. Now, Sir, while we make all these complaints about all our rights being denied and so on and so forth and about lawlessness in this country being at its zenith and our being deprived of the right to internal self-

determination and so on, we find Sir, there is a degree of arrogance, a degree of intolerance on the part of the Government in regard to these matters and this is reflected particularly in the way in which they deal with the Members of the international community. The first member of the international community who was given a dressing down is a Member of the UN staff, Mr. Allan Rock, Special Representative of the UN Secretary-General for Children in Armed Conflict. He came to this country; he went around; he had several things to say about various people and he said that children were being conscripted by paramilitary forces and that the security forces were being helpful to the paramilitary forces in carrying these out. It is common knowledge, it is known to everybody. We knew that in Batticaloa sometimes the security forces had round ups to enable these paramilitary forces to go and conscript children, to abduct children. Allan Rock merely said that, and he was hauled over the coals and he was called all manner of things. Then we had Sir John Holmes, UN Under Secretary-General for Humanitarian Affairs. He did not say anything very much. He came here, he looked around and then he quite correctly has said, I think, and quite truthfully said that Sri Lanka is one of the most dangerous places in the world for international aid workers. That is what he said. It is perfectly true because there have been a large number of aid workers who have been killed and then he was called a terrorist for saying that. It was said that he had taken a bribe from the LTTE . There was also a news report that he had been told that if he comes to Sri Lanka again that he will be dealt with. This is the way international personalities of the United Nations who come to this country, who see for themselves and speak out quite frankly and truthfully in the hope that the situation will improve are treated. In fact, I have a report which appeared in “The Sunday Times” of August 19th 2007 which states, I quote: “The UN Chief of Cabinet, Vijay Nambiar, ‘summoned Sri Lanka’s Permanent Representative to the United Nations, Prasad Kariyawasam. On behalf of the UN Secretary General, Nambiar asked Kariyawasam whether Fernandopulle’s remarks were the official view of the Sri Lankan Government. He had also referred to a Tamil website, which had attributed remarks to Fernandopulle that Sir John would be arrested if he visits Sri Lanka again.” I do not think Minister Mahinda Samarasinghe would have been a party to that arrest but this is what has been said by a Colleague of yours in Cabinet. It further states, I quote: “Kariawasam was to explain that the remarks were personal views of Fernandopulle and did not represent the Government.” That I will take with a pinch of salt because Fernandopulle is the Chief Government Whip, he is the person who speaks on behalf of the Government most in Parliament and I do not think he would have made such

[ගරු ආර්. සම්පන්දන් මහතා]

2007 ෙදසැම්බර් 12 3413 3414

very serious statements unless he had the approval of someone very high-up in the Government. He knew that he had the authority to speak in that way and speaking in that way would find acceptance with the Government and would be approved by the Government otherwise I do not think Fernandopulle would have dared to say that. Of course the UN Secretary-General was also very upset about this matter. He made a statement in regard to this matter. A newspaper report which appeared in the “Daily Mirror” of 18th August 2007 states, I quote: “Several government officials angrily rejected Holmes’ statement and demanded a retraction. Government Chief Whip and Minister Jeyaraj Fernandopulle on Wednesday called Mr. Holmes a “terrorist” and alleged he had taken a bribe from the LTTE” Naturally the UN Secretary General was very upset about it. The report further states, I quote: “UN Secretary-General Ban Ki-Moon said today that comments by a Sri Lankan Minister calling his humanitarian co-coordinator a “terrorist” were “unacceptable and unwarranted”. UN Humanitarian Chief John Holmes who was in Sri Lanka recently in an interview to Reuters said Sri Lanka was among the most dangerous places in the world for humanitarian workers. He specifically referred in particular to 17 aid workers attached to Action Against Hunger (ACF) killed execution-style in Eastern Sri Lanka an year ago.” The report goes on, Madam: “During his visit to the island nation, Mr. Holmes said nearly 30 aid workers have been killed over the past 18 months. The Consortium for Humanitarian Agencies, an umbrella group of 104 aid agencies operating in Sri Lanka, puts the number at 34, a figure the Government questions.” So what was wrong in Sir. John Holmes saying that Sri Lanka is one of the countries where the highest number of aid workers are killed. It is substantiated by very independent material. Then we have Justice Bhagwati, Chairman of the International Independent Group of Eminent Persons, a body which comprises of eminent people from various countries, from Bangladesh, from Indonesia, from Japan, from the US, from France, in fact we have met with some of them, having said that the Commission appointed to monitor certain human rights violations or to go into certain specific cases, which had been referred to that Commission and the Independent Group of Eminent persons appointed to oversee the working of the Commission cannot be a substitute for a robust mechanism permanently installed in this country to monitor human rights on a regular basis wherever it occurs in the country and Justice Bhagwati was hauled over the coals. I will not go into that in detail but the fact of the matter is that very responsible people in this country said very improper things, in my view, about Justice Bhagwati.

The language used was “The International Independent Group of Eminent Persons had engaged in improper conduct.” That was the language used. Justice Bhagwati called upon the Government to appoint a robust International Human Rights Monitoring Mechanism which had wider powers than the IIGEP. That is all that he wanted and he wanted that body to regularly monitor all human rights violations in this country by whomever they are committed and he was hauled over the coals for that. Now, Madam Chairperson, this is an indication of the arrogance, the insolence, the impertinence, the impudence, the intolerance, on the part of responsible persons in the Government in regard to statements made by very responsible persons whom you have invited, whom you have appointed to hold positions and when they speak the truth in regard to the actual situation you are unable to stomach it, you are unable to bear it and you insult these people. Now, recently, the UN Human Rights Commissioner, Madam Louise Arbour came here. I and some of my Colleagues also met with her, perhaps not as long as the Hon. Minister met with her, but we had a good meeting with her. She was of course, as everybody knows, a former prosecutor of the International Criminal Tribunal for former Yugoslavia and Rwanda. She was also a judge of the Supreme Court of Canada and this is what she has said after her visit to Sri Lanka. In fact, she was giving evidence in regard to the Sri Lankan situation before the UN Human Rights Council in Geneva. I have not been able to see what she said but I am inclined to the view that it could not have been too complimentary. Be that as it may, this is what she said when she came to Sri Lanka. "The Sunday Times" newspaper of 14th October, 2007 states, I quote: “Ms. Arbour, a former prosecutor of the International Criminal Tribunal for former Yugoslavia and Rwanda, expressed a different position when addressing the media after winding up her four day visit to Sri Lanka. She said- 'It has become apparent that pure technical co-operation cannot address what I consider are human rights challenges that the country faces at this time.' " She further states, I quote: “I want to make my position very clear. I believe that technical assistance or co-operation is always a good thing. But I don’t believe that it is sufficient at this particular stage in dealing with the human rights situation in Sri Lanka. I hope to continue my efforts to persuade the government that the presence of the OHCHR .in Sri Lanka would be a great benefit to the people.” She made a further statement. I quote: “A striking discrepancy exists in the perceptions of reality among different sections of the community. There are allegations that are easily dismissed as those told for propaganda purposes and so do not warrant investigation. I have had a lot of experience in creditability assessment and I have found in this

පාර්ලිෙම්න්තුව 3415 3416

country that many allegations, in my view, are certainly credible enough to be investigated.” The point that she made was that there were several allegations that were being made in this country, which are credible enough to be investigated but which were in fact not being investigated. That was the point she made. මූලාසනාරූඪ මන්තීතුමිය (தைலைமதாங்கும் உᾠப்பினர் அவர்கள்) (The Presiding Member) ගරු මන්තීතුමනි, ඔබතුමාට ෙවන් කර තිෙබන කාලය අවසානයි. ගරු ආර්. සම්පන්දන් මහතා (மாண்ᾗமிகு ஆர். சம்பந்தன்) (The Hon. R. Sampanthan) I have got 45 minutes, Madam. I started at - මූලාසනාරූඪ මන්තීතුමිය (தைலைமதாங்கும் உᾠப்பினர் அவர்கள்) (The Presiding Member) You have only 40 minutes. ගරු ආර්. සම්පන්දන් මහතා (மாண்ᾗமிகு ஆர். சம்பந்தன்) (The Hon. R. Sampanthan) She went on further, it states, I quote:

“Ms. Arbour who was in Sri Lanka on an invitation extended to her by President Mahinda Rajapaksa when the two met in Geneva earlier this year, said in her opening remarks, that in the context of the armed conflict and the emergency measures taken against terrorism, the weakness of the rule of law and prevalence of impunity in Sri Lanka were alarming. “While the Government pointed to several initiatives it has taken to address these issues, there has yet to be an adequate and credible public accounting for the vast majority of these incidents. In the absence of more vigorous investigations, prosecutions and convictions, it is hard to see how this will come to an end,” ….” I want to ask you, what has happened to the case of five students killed in Trincomalee. The file has been closed. I know that on the night of that killing there were efforts made to make it appear that the students were killed in a self-inflicted explosion. That theory exploded the next day when the JMO who held the postmortem revealed that every one of them was killed as a result of gunshot injuries. Bullets were recovered from the bodies of the children. If the proper guns had been recovered, the assailants would have been captured and would have been brought before the law. But the investigations were botched up. The proper guns were not recovered. That is what happened. When I met the President in regard to that matter, he told me "They were killed by the STF". He said, "I know that". I asked him, "How did the STF go there? They were never there". He said, "I do not know who sent them there". I said, "Your brother is the secretary. He should know". He said, "Even he did not know". The STF had suddenly gone there. They were never in Trincomalee. These five students were killed and thereafter they were called back. Then, what happened to the case of seventeen aid workers killed in Mutur? I have got the letter that I wrote to the President in regard to that matter. What is happening now? The bullets that were recovered as per the orders of the Anuradhapura Magistrate were not sent to the Government Analyst directly. The police went and took charge of the bullets from the doctor in Anuradhapura. The doctor in Anuradhapura should have sent the bullets to the Government Analyst or given the bullets to the court. But bullets were given to the police and the bullets were not in continuing proper safe custody. A senior police officer in charge of that investigation was suddenly transferred. What has happened to the murder of the Hon. Joseph Pararajasingham? What has happened to the murder of the Hon. Raviraj? They were our Members of Parliament. What happened to those investigations? The Hon. Raviraj was shot on a public highway, in a high security area. The assailants went past check posts. They got past check posts when they escaped. Why has not the truth been discovered? I do not say this. Ms. Louise Arbour says that proper investigations are called for. There must be a proper investigative mechanism. There must be a mechanism which oversees these matters which ensures that there are proper investigations, that these things are brought to light immediately, exposed immediately and then the persons concerned will realize that they cannot fudge, that they cannot deceive, that they must do a job of work or they must go home.

[ගරු ආර්. සම්පන්දන් මහතා]

2007 ෙදසැම්බර් 12 3417 3418

That is why, I think, Ms. Louise Arbour had been insisting upon a permanent UN Human Rights Mechanism which will be in a position to look at these matters but you are not concerned, you are not interested. I must also read, Madam, a statement which has been made recently by a very Senior Senator, a powerful US Senator, Senator Patrick Leahy who is the Chairman of the Senate Judiciary Committee and this was what he told the Senate when he made his statement. "The Sunday Times" of 4th November, 2007 has his speech. I quote: “ It is due to this information, from reputable sources, that the Senate attached three conditions to our assistance to the Sri Lankan military in the Fiscal Year 2008 State, Foreign Operations Appropriations bill. Anyone who reviews those conditions should agree that they are reasonable and appropriate. They would require the Sri Lankan government to be bringing to justice members of the military who have been credibly alleged to have committed gross violations of human rights; end unreasonable restrictions on access in the country by humanitarian organizations and journalists; and agree to the establishment of a field presence of the Office of the UN High Commissioner for Human Rights in Sri Lanka.” People cannot go freely and provide assistance to our refugees. Reputed international organizations, relief organizations that have served in this country and are servicing all parts of the world cannot go freely to our areas and provide relief to our people. Senator Patrick Leahy goes on to further say, Madam, I hope the Minister is listening: “ But rhetoric about human rights and the appointment of ineffectual commissions… I will repeat that. “…and the appointment of ineffectual commissions…” I am not saying it. Senator Leahy is saying it. “ ….commissions of inquiry that have no credibility, only goes so far. The situation remains grave and those responsible for abuses are rarely punished, making a peace agreement more difficult to achieve. A field presence of the Office of the High Commissioner for Human Rights, with sufficient mandate and capability to conduct full and unfettered monitoring throughout the country, communicate its findings to all sides of the conflict and the public, and provide advice and technical assistance, is overdue. Also urgently needed is greater access for humanitarian organizations to assist civilians caught in the cross-fire and for journalists to report the facts.” This is what we want, Madam. But, the Government would not do this. On the other hand, Madam, we find recently the UNICEF is under attack by some of my Colleagues here. They have got some meals ready to eat. They have got some meals for their own people. They serve widely in this country. They serve in all parts of this country and they are under attack, all motivated, to prevent the UNICEF continue their service to the Tamil people. Why are you doing all these? I need to pose the question as to why you are doing all these. I want to say that the reason why you are preventing an Independent United Nations Monitoring Mechanism in this country is not

merely because of the violations that have taken place thus far. This is a part of your larger political agenda. You have got an agenda of displacing the Tamils from the Eastern Province, a large scale displacement of Tamils. You have got an agenda of wanting to carry out an aggressive military programme irrespective of what will happen to the civilians in the Wanni, irrrespective of whether they will die in hundreds or thousands, you will not care. You want to kill them in order to succeed in your military programme. There is heavy aerial bombardment and heavy multi-barrel rocket fire. You want to move into Wanni and you want to kill those people. You do not mind the destruction that will be caused to civilian property. You will not mind the number of Civilian deaths. You do not mind hundreds or thousands of people being displaced. You do not care for those people. But you cannot do these things if you have in this country, a permanent UN human rights monitoring mechanism that will observe these things, will look into these things. That is the real truth. මූලාසනාරූඪ මන්තීතුමිය (தைலைமதாங்கும் உᾠப்பினர் அவர்கள்) (The Presiding Member) ගරු මන්තීතුමා, ඔබතුමා විනාඩි 10ක් වැඩිෙයන් අර ෙගන තිෙබනවා. ගරු ආර්. සම්පන්දන් මහතා (மாண்ᾗமிகு ஆர். சம்பந்தன்) (The Hon. R. Sampanthan) I will wind up in two minutes, Madam. In order to succeed in this agenda, you have to somehow keep an independent, impartial, upright and forthright monitoring mechanism out of the country in order to be able to pursue your agenda. This is the objective. I want to say, Madam, that this type of thing cannot be permitted. It must stop. If it does not stop, it will mean that - so far 600,000 Tamil people have being displaced - very soon yet another 500,000 will be displaced. Thousands of people will be killed. Tamil houses will be destroyed. Tamil means of livelihood will be destroyed. Their occupation will suffer. They will be driven to the refugee camps. There will be ethnic cleansing to pursue your programme of Sinhalisation of the East. You cannot do those things if your actions are monitored by an international body. That is the reason why you are not prepared to have this UN field mechanism. Therefore, I want to make an appeal to the Government, Madam. Stop this military pogrom, stop these attacks on the Tamil people, stop this aerial bombardment of Tamil areas which is indiscriminately killing Tamil civilians, stop using the multi-barrel rocket launchers in these areas, stop destroying our property, stop displacing our civilians, stop harassing us in this way and stop harming us in this way. Before I finish, Madam, please permit me to just read a statement made by His Excellency the President in the United Nations. You must know about it. I was a little

If you do not stop it, I want to make an appeal to the international community on the Floor of this House that we have a right to protection, we have a right to protection under international law and we want the international community not to be slow in ensuring that that right to protection under international law is made available to the Tamil civilian population in this country, because we have a right to live, we have a right to survive and we should not be allowed to perish. I thank you, Madam. [අ. භා. 3.24] ගරු රිසාඩ් බදියුදීන් මහතා (නැවත පදිංචි කිරීම හා ආපදා සහන ෙසේවා අමාතɕතුමා)

(மாண்ᾗமிகு றிஸாத் பதிᾜதீன் - மீள் குᾊயமர்த்ᾐைக, அனர்த்த நிவாரண ேசைவகள் அைமச்சர்) (The Hon. Risad Badhiutheen - Minister of Resettlement and Disaster Relief Services) බිස්මිල්ලාහිර් රහ්මානිර් රහීම් ගරු සුනිල් හඳුන්ෙනත්ති මහතා (மாண்ᾗமிகு சுனில் ஹந்ᾐன்ெனத்தி) (The Hon. Sunil Handunnetti) මූලාසනාරූඪ ගරු මන්තීතුමියනි, ඔබතුමියෙග් අවසරය ඇතිව ආරම්භෙය් දීම ගරු ඇමතිතුමාට ෙපොඩි කාරණාවක් මා මතු කරන්නට කැමැතියි. නැවත පදිංචි කිරීම හා ආපදා සහන ෙසේවා අමාතɕාංශ ය යටෙත් මැතිවරණවලින් පචණ්ඩ කියාවලට

[ගරු ආර්. සම්පන්දන් මහතා]

2007 ෙදසැම්බර් 12 3421 3422

ெசய்ேதாம் என்பᾐம் உலகம் அறிந்த உண்ைமயாகும். இவ்வாறாக மீள்குᾊேயற்ற நடவᾊக்ைககளின்ெபாᾨᾐ அவர்கᾦக்குத் ேதைவயான உட்கட்டைமப்ᾗ வசதிகைளᾜம், அவர்கᾦக்கு ஏற்பட்ட இழப்ᾗக்கᾦக்கான இழப்பீᾌகைள வழங்கும் நடவᾊக்ைககைளᾜம் எᾐவித இன, மத, ேபத ேவᾠபாᾌம் இன்றிச் ெசய்ᾐவᾞகின்ேறாம். கடந்த காலத்தில் மட்டக்களப்ᾗ மாவட்டத்தில் ஏற்பட்ட ᾜத்த சூழ்நிைல காரணமாக இடம்ெபயர்ந்த மக்களில் ஏறத்தாழ 36,343 குᾌம்பங்கள் வᾫணதீᾫ, ெசங்கலᾊ, கிரான், பட்ᾊப்பைள, ெவல்லாெவளி மற்ᾠம் வாகைர ேபான்ற பிரேதச ெசயலாளர் பிாிᾫகளில் மீள்குᾊேயற்றம் ெசய்யப்பட்ᾌள்ளனர். இதில் ெமாத்தமாக 1,19,434 தனிநபர்கள் அடங்குகின்றனர். இேதேபான்ᾠ, கிழக்கு மாகாணத்தின் மற்ᾠெமாᾞ மாவட்டமாகிய திᾞேகாணமைல மாவட்டத்தில் ெவᾞகல், ᾚᾑர், ேசᾞவில, ஈச்சிலம்பற்ᾠ ேபான்ற பிரேதச ெசயலாளர் பிாிᾫகᾦக்குட்பட்ட பகுதிகளில் 12,000 குᾌம்பங்கᾦக்கும் ேமற்பட்ட கிட்டத்தட்ட ஐம்பதாயிரம் நபர்கள் மீள்குᾊேயற்றம் ெசய்யப்பட்ᾌள்ளனர். ᾜத்தத்தினால் பாதிக்கப்பட்ᾌ இடம்ெபயர்ந்த, இடம்ெபயர்க்கப்பட்ட மக்கள் ஒப்பீட்ᾌ ாீதியில் அதிகளவில் காணப்பᾌவᾐ வட மாகாணத்திலாகும். பல இலட்சக்கணக்கான சேகாதர தமிழ் மக்கள் இம்மாகாணத்திேல இடம்ெபயர்ந்திᾞக்கின்றார்கள். அேதேவைள, நான் பிரதிநிதித்ᾐவப்பᾌத்ᾐகின்ற வட மாகாண ᾙஸ்ᾢம் சᾚகம் பலாத்காரமாக அங்கிᾞந்ᾐ ெவளிேயற்றப்பட்ᾌ கடந்த 17 ஆண்ᾌகளாகப் ᾗத்தளத்திᾤம் நாட்ᾊன் ஏைனய சில மாவட்டங்களிᾤம் இன்ேனாரன்ன இன்னல்கᾦக்கு ᾙகம்ெகாᾌத்ᾐ வாழ்ந்ᾐ வᾞகின்ற ᾐன்பியல் வரலாᾠ யாவᾞம் அறிந்தேத. ெகளரவ தைலைமதாங்கும் உᾠப்பினர் அவர்கேள, கிழக்கு மாகாணத்தில் அரசாங்கத்திற்கு ஏற்பட்ட சாதகமான சூழ்நிைல காரணமாக பாதிக்கப்பட்ட மக்கைள அங்கு மீள்குᾊேயற்றம் ெசய்வதில், அவர்களᾐ இயல்ᾗ வாழ்க்ைக நிைலைய மீளக்ெகாண்ᾌ வᾞவதில் நாம் கணிசமானளᾫ ெவற்றி அைடந்ᾐள்ேளாம். ஆனால், வட மாகாணத்திேல ெதாடர்ந்ᾐவᾞம் ᾜத்த சூழ்நிைல காரணமாக அவ்வாறான மீள்குᾊேயற்றத்ைதᾜம் அதேனாᾌ ெதாடர்ᾗபட்ட மக்களின் இயல்ᾗ வாழ்க்ைக நிைலையᾜம் மீளக்ெகாண்ᾌ வᾞவதில் நாம் சில நைடᾙைறச் சிக்கல்கைள எதிர்ேநாக்கிக் ெகாண்ᾊᾞக்கின்ேறாம். මූලාසනාරූඪ මන්තීතුමිය (தைலைமதாங்கும் உᾠப்பினர் அவர்கள்) (The Presiding Member) ගරු මන්තීතුමා, කරුණාකර ෙපොඩ්ඩක් නිශ්ශබ්ද ෙවන්න. ෙම් අවස්ථාෙව්දී ගරු ගයන්ත කරුණාතිලක මන්තීතුමා මූලාසනය ගන්නවා ඇති. අනතුරුව ගරු ෙර්ණුකා ෙහේරත් මහත්මිය මූලාසනෙයන් ඉවත් වූෙයන් ගරු ගයන්ත කරුණාතිලක මහතා මූලාසනාරූඪ විය.

அதன்பிறகு, மாண்ᾗமிகு (திᾞமதி) ேரᾎகா ேஹரத் அவர்கள் அக்கிராசனத்தினின்ᾠ அகலேவ, மாண்ᾗமிகு கயந்த கᾞணாதிலக்க அவர்கள் தைலைம வகித்தார்கள். Whereupon THE HON. (MRS.) RENUKA HERATH left the Chair and THE HON. GAYANTHA KARUNATILLEKA took the Chair. ගරු රිසාඩ් බදියුදීන් මහතා (மாண்ᾗமிகு றிஸாத் பதிᾜதீன்) (The Hon. Risad Badhiutheen ) எனிᾔம், இடம்ெபயர்ந்ᾐ தற்ெபாᾨᾐ நானாட்டான், ᾙᾞங்கன் ேபான்ற பிரேதசங்களிேல வாழ்ந்ᾐ வᾞகின்ற மன்னார் மாவட்டத்தின் ெதன்பகுதியான சிலாவத்ᾐைறப் பிரேதச மக்கைளᾜம் அேதேபால், ᾗத்தளம் மாவட்டத்திேல அதிகமானளவில் வாழ்ந்ᾐ வᾞகின்ற அந்தப் பிரேதசத்ைதச் ேசர்ந்த ᾙஸ்ᾢம் மக்கைளᾜம் மிக விைரவிேல பாᾐகாப்ᾗத் தரப்பினாின் உத்தரவாதம் கிைடக்கப்ெபற்றᾐம் அந்தந்தப் பிரேதசங்களிேல மீள்குᾊேயற்றம் ெசய்கின்ற பணிைய நாங்கள்

ᾙன்ெனᾌக்கவிᾞக்கின்ேறாம். வட மாகாணத்தில் மக்கைள மீள் குᾊேயற்றம் ெசய்வதில் சில நைடᾙைறச் சிக்கல்கள் இᾞந்தாᾤம்கூட, அந்த மாவட்டங்களிேல வாᾨகின்ற ᾜத்தத்தினால் பாதிக்கப்பட்ட மக்களின் அத்தியாவசியத் ேதைவகைளப் ᾘர்த்தி ெசய்வதில் எமᾐ அைமச்சு ஒᾞ பாாிய பங்களிப்ைபச் ெசய்ᾐ வᾞகின்றைமைய யாᾞம் மᾠக்க ᾙᾊயாᾐ. உதாரணமாக, வட மாகாணத்ைதச் ேசர்ந்த ஐந்ᾐ நிர்வாக மாவட்டங்களிᾤம் வாᾨகின்ற பல இலட்சக்கணக்கான மக்கᾦக்கு உலர் உணᾫகைள நாம் விநிேயாகம் ெசய்ᾐ வᾞகின்ேறாம். 2007ஆம் ஆண்ᾊல் மட்ᾌம் அாிசி, மா, சீனி மற்ᾠம் பᾞப்ᾗ ேபான்ற உலர் உணᾫப் ெபாᾞட்கᾦக்காக யாழ்ப்பாண மாவட்டத்திற்கு 499 மில்ᾢயன் ᾟபாᾫம், கிளிெநாச்சி மாவட்டத்திற்கு 216 மில்ᾢயன் ᾟபாᾫம், ᾙல்ைலத்தீᾫ மாவட்டத்திற்கு 228 மில்ᾢயன் ᾟபாᾫம், மன்னார் மாவட்டத்திற்கு 44 மில்ᾢயன் ᾟபாᾫம், வᾫனியா மாவட்டத்திற்கு 32 மில்ᾢயன் ᾟபாᾫம் அந்தந்த மாவட்ட நிர்வாகங்களின் ஊடாக ெசலᾫ ெசய்யப்பட்ᾊᾞக்கின்றᾐ. ெகளரவ நாடாᾦமன்ற உᾠப்பினர் சிவாஜிᾢங்கம் அவர்கள், வட மாகாணத்ᾐக்கு நிவாரண உதவிகைள வழங்குவதில்ைலெயன்ற ஒᾞ குற்றச்சாட்ᾊைன ᾙன்ைவத்திᾞந்தார். ஆனால், 2007ஆம் ஆண்ᾊல் மாத்திரம் வட மாகாணத்தில் உலர் உணᾫ விநிேயாக நடவᾊக்ைககᾦக்காக 1,019 மில்ᾢயன் ᾟபா ஒᾐக்கீᾌ ெசய்யப்பட்ᾊᾞக்கின்றெதன்பைத இந்த உயர் சைபயிேல நான் கூறிக்ெகாள்ள விᾞம்ᾗகின்ேறன். இைவயைனத்ᾐம் அரசாங்க அதிபர்களின் ஊடாக அந்த மக்கᾦக்கு பகிர்ந்தளிக்கப்பட்டன. ගරු සිවනාදන් කිෙෂෝර් මහතා (மாண்ᾗமிகு சிவநாதன் கிேஷார்) (The Hon. Sivanathan Kissor) Sir, I rise to a point of Order. ගරු රිසාඩ් බදියුදීන් මහතා (மாண்ᾗமிகு றிஸாத் பதிᾜதீன்) (The Hon. Risad Badhiutheen ) Yes. ගරු සිවනාදන් කිෙෂෝර් මහතා (மாண்ᾗமிகு சிவநாதன் கிேஷார்) (The Hon. Sivanathan Kissor) ெகளரவ அைமச்சர் அவர்கேள, சிவாஜிᾢங்கம் அவர்கள் என்ன ெசான்னார் என்றால், —

ගරු රිසාඩ් බදියුදීන් මහතා (மாண்ᾗமிகு றிஸாத் பதிᾜதீன்) (The Hon. Risad Badhiutheen ) ெகளரவ கிேஷார் அவர்கேள, அவர் ெசால்ᾤம்ெபாᾨᾐ நீங்கள் சைபயில் இᾞக்கவில்ைல. அᾐ ஒᾞ point of Order அல்ல. அந்த விடயம் பற்றிᾜம் ெசால்லவிᾞக்கின்ேறன். எனேவ, ெகாஞ்சம் ெபாᾠைமயாகக் ேகᾦங்கள்!

ගරු සිවනාදන් කිෙෂෝර් මහතා (மாண்ᾗமிகு சிவநாதன் கிேஷார்) (The Hon. Sivanathan Kissor) Please! அதற்குத்தான் ெசால்கின்ேறன், ெகாஞ்சம் இைதக் ேகᾦங்கள்! அவர் என்ன ெசான்னார் என்றால், இந்தப் பகுதி மக்கள் குண்ᾌ ெவᾊப்பில் ெசத்தᾫடன் நீங்கள் ஆஸ்பத்திாிக்குப் ேபாய் நஷ்டஈட்ᾌக் ெகாᾌப்பனᾫ ெகாᾌக்கின்றீர்கள் என்ᾠம், அப்பகுதிகளில் விமானக் குண்ᾌத் தாக்குதல்கள் நடந்ᾐ மக்கள் ெசத்தால் அதற்கு நஷ்டஈட்ᾌக் ெகாᾌப்பனᾫகள் ெகாᾌப்பதில்ைலெயன்ᾠம்தான் அவர் ெசான்னார்.

ගරු රිසාඩ් බදියුදීන් මහතා (மாண்ᾗமிகு றிஸாத் பதிᾜதீன்) (The Hon. Risad Badhiutheen ) அவர் ேபசும்ேபாᾐ நான் நிைனக்கின்ேறன், நீங்கள் இங்ேக சைபயிᾔள்ேள இᾞக்கவில்ைல என்ᾠ.
